123:         <h3 style="font-size:18px; font-weight:600; color:var(--char); margin-bottom:12px;">If we have a visit on the books</h3>
124:         <div style="font-size:14px; color:var(--stone); line-height:1.75; margin-bottom:32px;">
125:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;">Life happens. If you need to move our visit, just text me at (323) 433-1350 — the earlier the better. Anything 48 hours out or more, no problem at all, we'll find a new time.</p>
126:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;">Inside 48 hours I ask that the booked time be paid for, because that slot was held for you and I usually can't refill it last-minute. Same for no-shows. I'd rather you tell me you're overwhelmed and we reschedule than ghost the appointment — I genuinely won't be weird about it.</p>
127:           <p style="margin-bottom:0;">Hourly sessions and flex blocks are paid at booking. Flex-block hours don't expire — they sit there until you need them. If something about a visit didn't sit right, text me within a week and we'll talk it through directly.</p>
128:         </div>
129:         <h3 style="font-size:18px; font-weight:600; color:var(--char); margin-bottom:12px;">Resale, consignment & online buyers</h3>
130:         <div style="font-size:14px; color:var(--stone); line-height:1.75;">
131:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;"><strong style="color:var(--char);">All resale sales are final.</strong> Items are sold as-described with photos, measurements, and condition notes. No returns, no refunds, no exchanges, no chargebacks. Buyers are responsible for reading the listing in full before purchasing.</p>
132:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;"><strong style="color:var(--char);">Authenticity & condition.</strong> Designer items are inspected and described in good faith. If you have questions about authenticity or condition, ask before you buy — not after. Once an item ships, the sale is closed.</p>
133:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;"><strong style="color:var(--char);">Shipping & risk.</strong> Items ship insured when value warrants it. Risk of loss transfers to the buyer at hand-off to the carrier. Claims for lost or damaged shipments are filed with the carrier, not with The Well Lived Citizen.</p>
134:           <p style="margin-bottom:16px;"><strong style="color:var(--char);">Consignment (seller side).</strong> Curated Resale is a service performed on behalf of the client. The client retains ownership of items until sold. Commission is calculated on net proceeds after platform and processing fees, per the signed resale agreement. Payouts follow the schedule in that agreement.</p>
135:           <p style="margin-bottom:0;"><strong style="color:var(--char);">Chargebacks & disputes.</strong> Buyers who file a chargeback without first contacting me to resolve the issue will be reported to the platform and blocked from future purchases. Disputes are handled by text or email first — that's almost always faster than a bank.</p>
136:         </div>

File: Visual-Brand-main/artifacts/website/vite.config.ts
================
  1: import { defineConfig, type Plugin } from "vite";
  2: import path from "path";
  3: import fs from "fs";
  4: import { execFileSync } from "child_process";
  5: const rawPort = process.env.PORT ?? "5000";
  6: const port = Number(rawPort);
  7: if (Number.isNaN(port) || port <= 0) throw new Error(`Invalid PORT value: "${rawPort}"`);
  8: const basePath = process.env.BASE_PATH ?? "/";
  9: const root = path.resolve(import.meta.dirname);
 10: const SITE_ORIGIN = "https://thewelllivedcitizen.com";
 11: type SitemapEntry = { loc: string; file: string; changefreq?: string; priority?: number };
 12: const SITEMAP_ENTRIES: SitemapEntry[] = [
 13:   { loc: "/", file: "index.html", changefreq: "weekly", priority: 1.0 },
 14:   { loc: "/about", file: "about.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.7 },
 15:   { loc: "/services", file: "services.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.9 },
 16:   { loc: "/pricing", file: "pricing.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.8 },
 17:   { loc: "/contact", file: "contact.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.7 },
 18:   { loc: "/services/home-organization", file: "services/home-organization.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.8 },
 19:   { loc: "/services/legacy", file: "services/legacy.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.8 },
 20:   { loc: "/services/house-calls", file: "services/house-calls.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.8 },
 21:   { loc: "/services/resale", file: "services/resale.html", changefreq: "monthly", priority: 0.8 },
 22: ];
 23: function getLastModISO(absFile: string): string {
 24:   try {
 25:     const out = execFileSync("git", ["log", "-1", "--format=%cI", "--", absFile], {
 26:       cwd: root,
 27:       stdio: ["ignore", "pipe", "ignore"],
 28:     })
 29:       .toString()
 30:       .trim();
 31:     if (out) {
 32:       return out.slice(0, 10);
 33:     }
 34:   } catch {
 35:   }
 36:   try {
 37:     const stat = fs.statSync(absFile);
 38:     return stat.mtime.toISOString().slice(0, 10);
 39:   } catch {
 40:     return new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10);
 41:   }
 42: }
 43: function escapeXml(s: string): string {
 44:   return s.replace(/[<>&'"]/g, (c) =>
 45:     c === "<" ? "&lt;" : c === ">" ? "&gt;" : c === "&" ? "&amp;" : c === "'" ? "&apos;" : "&quot;",
 46:   );
 47: }
 48: function buildSitemap(): string {
 49:   const urls = SITEMAP_ENTRIES.map((e) => {
 50:     const lastmod = getLastModISO(path.resolve(root, e.file));
 51:     const loc = escapeXml(SITE_ORIGIN + e.loc);
 52:     const parts = [`    <loc>${loc}</loc>`, `    <lastmod>${lastmod}</lastmod>`];
 53:     if (e.changefreq) parts.push(`    <changefreq>${e.changefreq}</changefreq>`);
 54:     if (typeof e.priority === "number") parts.push(`    <priority>${e.priority.toFixed(1)}</priority>`);
 55:     return `  <url>\n${parts.join("\n")}\n  </url>`;
 56:   }).join("\n");
 57:   return `<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>\n<urlset xmlns="http://www.sitemaps.org/schemas/sitemap/0.9">\n${urls}\n</urlset>\n`;
 58: }
 59: function buildRobots(): string {
 60:   return `User-agent: *\nAllow: /\nDisallow: /admin\nDisallow: /admin.html\n\nSitemap: ${SITE_ORIGIN}/sitemap.xml\n`;
 61: }
 62: function seoFilesPlugin(): Plugin {
 63:   let outDir = path.resolve(root, "dist/public");
 64:   return {
 65:     name: "well-lived-citizen-seo-files",
 66:     apply: "build",
 67:     configResolved(config) {
 68:       outDir = path.resolve(config.root, config.build.outDir);
 69:     },
 70:     writeBundle() {
 71:       fs.mkdirSync(outDir, { recursive: true });
 72:       fs.writeFileSync(path.join(outDir, "sitemap.xml"), buildSitemap(), "utf8");
 73:       fs.writeFileSync(path.join(outDir, "robots.txt"), buildRobots(), "utf8");
 74:     },
 75:   };
 76: }
 77: export default defineConfig({
 78:   base: basePath,
 79:   root,
 80:   appType: "mpa",
 81:   plugins: [seoFilesPlugin()],
 82:   build: {
 83:     outDir: path.resolve(root, "dist/public"),
 84:     emptyOutDir: true,
 85:     rollupOptions: {
 86:       input: {
 87:         index: path.resolve(root, "index.html"),
 88:         about: path.resolve(root, "about.html"),
 89:         services: path.resolve(root, "services.html"),
 90:         pricing: path.resolve(root, "pricing.html"),
 91:         contact: path.resolve(root, "contact.html"),
 92:         admin: path.resolve(root, "admin.html"),
 93:         homeOrganization: path.resolve(root, "services/home-organization.html"),
 94:         legacy: path.resolve(root, "services/legacy.html"),
 95:         houseCalls: path.resolve(root, "services/house-calls.html"),
 96:         resale: path.resolve(root, "services/resale.html"),
 97:       },
 98:     },
 99:   },
100:   server: {
101:     port,
102:     host: "0.0.0.0",
103:     allowedHosts: true,
104:     fs: { strict: true, deny: ["**/.*"] },
105:   },
106:   preview: {
107:     port,
108:     host: "0.0.0.0",
109:     allowedHosts: true,
110:   },
111: });

 16: ## DAY 1 — Open the door (founder intro / "there has to be an easier way")

 18: **Instagram caption**

 20: 
 21: I'm Dayna. I run The Well Lived Citizen out of Los Angeles. I help people land in homes that actually work for the lives they're living now — not the life they had ten years ago, not the life that fits in a magazine.
 22: 
 23: Closets that no longer match your body, your season, or how you actually get dressed. Moves where the boxes made it through the door and nothing feels settled. Storage units you only visit to make sure they weren't broken into. The drawer of cords. The room that keeps catching everything.
 24: 
 25: I'm built for your chaos.
 26: 
 27: Text me — (323) 433-1350.
 28: 
 29: **Facebook version**
 30: A client in Seattle once said it out loud — "there has to be an easier way" — and that became a business.
 31: 
 32: I'm Dayna Brown. I run The Well Lived Citizen out of Los Angeles. For the last fifteen years I've been the person who solves invisible problems for big companies — moving operations, fixing systems, building the structures behind the scenes that make the day actually work.
 33: 
 34: Now I do it for people. Inside their homes. The closet that doesn't fit your life anymore. The move where the boxes arrived but nothing feels settled. The drawer no one opens. The storage unit you've been paying on for two years.
 35: 
 36: It is not magazine organizing. It is not the perfect Pinterest pantry. It is the relief of a room that finally works the way you actually live in it.

 44: ## DAY 2 — Gayle (the woman across the hall)
 45: 
 46: **Instagram caption**
 47: A woman lived across the hall from me for years. We started as people who said hello at the mailbox. She became one of the most independent women I've ever known — 84, post-hip surgery, full life behind her, full life still ahead.
 48: 
 49: What I noticed about Gayle: people naturally wanted to make life easier for her. Not because she demanded it. Because there's a way of moving through the world that makes others want to say, "I can take care of that for you."
 50: 
 51: I started doing the small things. The new TV. The thermostat. The smart-home stuff that wasn't smart yet. A clicker for the lamps that lived on her bedside table at night and the dresser by the door in the morning.
 52: 
 53: That's where this business comes from. Not everyone has a Gayle. Not everyone has the neighbor. Sometimes you just need the person who knows what to do.
 54: 
 55: Text me — (323) 433-1350.
 56: 
 57: **Facebook version**
 58: There was a woman who lived across the hall from me for years. Gayle. We started as the kind of neighbors who waved at the mailbox. Then one day we were friends.
 59: 
 60: She was 84 when I knew her best. Post-hip surgery. Independent in a way most people aren't even at thirty. She didn't ask for much, ever. But there was something about her — about the way she moved through her own life with grace and curiosity — that made everyone around her want to quietly remove friction.
 61: 
 62: So I did. I set up her TV with one clicker so she could get to the channels she actually watched. I put a remote for the lamps on her bedside table at night, and she'd move it to the dresser by the door in the morning so she could light the whole room from the doorway when she came home. Her closet was arranged by item and color so she could see what she had and choose accordingly. The heat was set just right.
 63: 
 64: She wrote me later: "Thank you for making life easier for me."
 65: 
 66: That sentence is the entire reason this business exists. Most of us don't have a Gayle's neighbor. Most of us don't have anyone who notices the small things. The Well Lived Citizen is me being that person, professionally, in Los Angeles.
 67: 
 68: Text me — (323) 433-1350.

 74: ## DAY 3 — The flood (why this work is what it is)
 75: 
 76: **Instagram caption**
 77: A year ago I lived through a flood. I moved through 13 temporary homes in a single year. My dog lived in a storage unit beside me for some of it. Years of belongings — gone or damaged.
 78: 
 79: What surprised me wasn't the loss. It was the disorientation of living without the things that quietly reflect you back to yourself every day. The art on the wall. The clothes in the closet. The objects that make a place feel like the life you built.
 80: 
 81: Someone stepped in for me during that season. On paper she was a "home organizer." What she actually did was hold the decisions I was too depleted to make. She was relief.
 82: 
 83: That changed how I understand this work.
 84: 
 85: If something in your life right now needs someone to step in and quietly carry the weight — text me. (323) 433-1350.
 86: 
 87: **Facebook version**
 88: About a year ago, I lived through a flood. Not metaphorical. Water. Real loss. I moved through 13 temporary homes and Airbnbs in a single year. My dog spent part of that time in a storage unit beside me. A lot of what I owned — irreplaceable things — was damaged or just gone.
 89: 
 90: Here's what I didn't expect: the disorientation. Not just the grief. The destabilizing feeling of waking up without the things that reflect you back to yourself. The art on the wall. The clothes in the closet. The bowl on the counter you've used every morning for ten years. They are not just stuff. They are the quiet evidence of the life you built.
 91: 
 92: I am someone who has always been the capable one. The fixer. The one who moves through complexity with calm. But during that season I met my limit. The decisions were too many. The losses were too fresh.
 93: 
 94: Someone stepped in. On paper she would have been called a home organizer. What she actually did was sit with me through decisions I couldn't make alone. She held the operational weight while I held the grief. She was relief.
 95: 
 96: That's what I do now, professionally, in Los Angeles. Not to make your home look perfect. To help you keep moving forward when something has stopped, or shifted, or quietly gotten too heavy.
 97: 
 98: Text me — (323) 433-1350.

For the rest, we organize, find homes, and make easy plans — so the weight of "things" never falls on the people you love at the worst possible moment.

149: Bags, coats, watches, jewelry, the kid stuff that's still in the box. If you'd quietly like it gone and converted to cash, I'm the person.

You haven't sold it because the *actual work* of selling it — photos, measurements, platform research, buyer questions, returns, strangers offering you $40 for a $1,200 bag — is more energy than you have on a Tuesday night.
157: 
158: So I made it small. Text one photo to (323) 433-1350. I'll quote a pickup this week and tell you honestly what it would likely list for. **No agreement until you see the number.** If the number's worth it to you, I take it from there: pickup, styling, measurements, listings, buyer questions, returns, monthly check-ins, payout on an agreed split. A closed closet door isn't just storage when it tells the story of a marriage, a season of confidence, the person someone once was.

File: Visual-Brand-main/attached_assets/BRAND-MATCH-MARKETING-PROGRAM.md
================
  1: # Brand-Match Marketing Program — The Well Lived Citizen Co
  2: **Source:** Yesterday's strategy session (Apr 16, ~5pm PT)
  3: **Status:** Locked source-of-truth for all social content across all three accounts.
  4: **Supersedes:** The earlier `10-day-launch-content.md` draft (which was written without this program in context and should be discarded).
  5: 
  6: ---
  7: 
  8: ## THE THREE VOICES (and what each account is for)
  9: 
 10: ### @thewelllivedcitizen — Company
 11: - **Job:** positioning + lead gen for House Calls, Org/Modern Move, Legacy. People follow this account because they trust you, not because they want to buy a sweater.
 12: - **Voice:** calm, observant, dry, slightly literary. Notices a thing, names it, doesn't moralize. No exclamation points. Em-dashes welcome. Short sentences mixed with one long one. Sentence case.
 13: - **Forbidden:** hustle language ("DM to book!"), girlboss energy, before/after grids, stock photos, motivational quotes, emoji.
 14: - **Allowed:** real moments, fragments, observations about modern life, the gap you fill.
 15: 
 16: ### @thewelllivedcloset — Closet
 17: - **Job:** drive sales (Poshmark/eBay) + intake (people sending you bags). This is the cash account.
 18: - **Voice:** same register, slightly more connoisseur. Story-led, never bargain-led. The piece is a vehicle for a chapter. You're the eye and the steward, not the reseller.
 19: - **Forbidden:** "OBO," "make me an offer," "must go," "DEAL," haul language, fast-fashion energy.
 20: - **Allowed:** provenance, year, who wore it, why it matters, sizing in the same breath. Honesty about condition.
 21: 
 22: ### @welldressedcitizen — Archive
 23: - **Job:** one transition post, then dark. Catches your existing audience and forwards them.
 24: - **Voice:** brief, warm, final. Two paragraphs max.
 25: 
 26: ---
 27: 
 28: ## VISUAL SYSTEM (the same across all three accounts)
 29: 
 30: - **Palette:** cream `#F5F0E8`, warm `#FAF7F2`, linen `#EDE7DB`, charcoal `#1C1917`, rust `#9A5B3C`. Nothing else. No bright colors, no white-white, no black-black.
 31: - **Light:** natural daylight only. No flash. Shoot in the morning or late afternoon. North-facing window if you have one.
 32: - **Backgrounds:** linen, raw wood, plaster wall, cream sheet. Never a busy room, never carpet, never your bed.
 33: - **Composition:** one subject per image. Flat lay or hanger or in-context (the smoke detector, the labeled box, the binder). Lots of negative space.
 34: - **Faces:** no client faces. Hands and objects only. You can show your own hands working.
 35: - **Filters:** none. If you want, drop saturation 5–10% for a quieter look. That's it.
 36: - **Format:** 4:5 portrait for feed posts (most real estate). Square only for grid coherence. Stories are 9:16.
 37: - **Type on graphics:** Plus Jakarta Sans, charcoal on cream, lowercase or sentence case. Never all caps.
 38: 
 39: ---
 40: 
 41: ## CAPTION ARCHITECTURE
 42: 
 43: ### Company posts — 3-part formula
 44: 1. **The moment** (1–3 sentences). Concrete, specific, no abstraction.
 45: 2. **The gap it points to** (1–2 sentences). Quietly names what's actually going on under the surface.
 46: 3. **The soft handoff** (1 line). Where to find you. No exclamation.
 47: 
 48: ### Closet posts — 5-line spec
 49: 1. **The piece** — designer, year if known, what it is. One line.
 50: 2. **The story** — provenance, who wore it, where it lived. 1–3 sentences.
 51: 3. **The fit** — size, measurements, condition honestly stated.
 52: 4. **The platform** — Poshmark or eBay, link in bio.
 53: 5. **The cross-tag** — `@thewelllivedcitizen` at the end so the two accounts feed each other.
 54: 
 55: ### Hashtags
 56: - 3–5 max, never more. Mix:
 57:   - one local (`#losangeles`, `#lavintage`)
 58:   - one platform (`#poshmarkambassador`, `#ebayfinds`)
 59:   - one niche (`#vintageysl`, `#consignmentla`)
 60: - Never lifestyle-influencer hashtags (`#blessed`, `#girlboss`, `#entrepreneurlife`).
 61: 
 62: ---
 63: 
 64: ## WHAT TO NEVER DO (across all accounts)
 65: - No before/afters. Your work is not a transformation product.
 66: - No "DM to book." The site exists. Send people to the site.
 67: - No begging language ("please share," "tag a friend," "save this post").
 68: - No selfie content. You are the eye behind the work, not the influencer.
 69: - No carousel posts longer than 4 slides.
 70: - No reels with trending audio that isn't yours. Voice notes over silent footage > viral sounds.
 71: - No emoji.
 72: - Never post the same item across both accounts on the same day. Closet stays closet.
 73: 
 74: ---
 75: 
 76: ## CADENCE (sustainable, not heroic)
 77: - **Closet:** 4–5x per week. Each new arrival = 1 feed post + 1 story. This is your sales engine.
 78: - **Company:** 2–3x per week. One ethos post, one real-life moment, one service mention with story.
 79: - **Stories on both:** daily if you can, even if it's just one frame.
 80: - **Reels:** 1 per week per account, max. Don't chase. Use voice notes over object footage.
 81: - **Posting times:** 9–10am or 6–8pm Pacific. Skip mid-afternoon.
 82: 
 83: ---
 84:

 1: WEEK 1 — Turn the site into a cash machine (this is the one that matters)
 2: 
 3: The current site is calm and credible. It's not built to convert a stressed millennial at 10pm on their phone. Five changes that move the needle in days:
 4: 
 5: Text-first CTA everywhere. Replace the primary "Get in Touch" button with "Text me — (323) 433‑1350" as the fastest action, form as secondary. A text conversation closes in hours; a form sits in an inbox. Every page hero, every service card.
 6: One‑click resale intake. The current "Commission-based · agreement required" is friction at exactly the wrong moment. Add a fast‑path subline: "Got a bag? Send a photo to (323) 433‑1350. I'll quote pickup this week. Agreement only after you see what I'd list." Lowers the bar from commit to send me a photo.
 7: Bookable house call slot. A named offer: "2‑hour House Call — $350, book this week." Fixed price, no quote, calendar link. One-tap buy. This is the Gayle-next-door service productized for the millennial phone.
 8: Free 15‑min conversation link. Cal.com or Calendly free tier. Embed on Contact, link from every CTA. Converts "not sure yet" into a scheduled call without a gatekeeper form.
 9: Payment rails visible. Venmo/Zelle handle + Stripe payment link on Contact and on the Services page — so first-time clients can deposit on the phone the same day. Stripe payment links take 10 minutes to set up.
10: None of this touches your voice or brand. It just removes friction between a warm lead and your bank account. If I do only Tier 1, you get paying work inside 7–10 days.
11: 
12: WEEK 1 PARALLEL — Get found for free (2 hours of work, big compounding)
13: 
14: Google Business Profile — Los Angeles, service‑area business. Free. Takes 60 minutes. Indexable within days. This is how Gayle's daughter finds you at 11pm.
15: Nextdoor profile in your current LA neighborhoods. This is Gayle's literal channel. Free. One post introducing yourself.
16: Instagram bio standardized to one sentence that you repeat everywhere. Same bio on IG, TikTok, Nextdoor, GBP. So every platform funnels to the same phone number and site.
17: 10 referral texts. Not a mass message. Ten specific LA humans who know your work, each told the same three things: I'm live, here's the link, here's who I help — ask them to send one person. Highest-converting channel you have for free.
18: No Thumbtack, no TaskRabbit, no new platforms you have to feed. You've been burned there. Don't rebuild that energy drain.
19: 
20: WEEK 2 — Credibility moves that feed the income flow
21: 
22: One pinned Instagram video. You, talking to camera, 60 seconds, the fur coat story or the Gayle smoke detector story. Not a pitch — a story. That's your entire marketing. Doesn't need production. Phone, face, one take.
23: "A few of the stories" section on the site. A small page — maybe 3 entries — each is one object + its chapter. The fur. The broken China. An Alexa night. Not case studies. Fragments. This is how you seed the Well Dressed Citizen storyline without needing the storefront yet. It's also the single best SEO/shareable page you can have — nobody else has copy like this.
24: One testimonial. Gayle if she'll give one. Anybody. One line is enough. Trust-built business needs one visible piece of trust on the homepage.
25: WEEK 3 — The positioning move that reframes the whole site
26: 
27: One new band on the home page, under the hero, ~80 words: the thesis. Names the gap you've been describing — the neighbor we don't have anymore, the objects our lives weren't built for, the trusted person you could actually call. This is the line that separates you from every organizer/handyman/estate service on Google. I'd write a draft, you'd keyword-level it, we'd ship it.
28: 
29: And the Legacy card reframe — not today, Week 3. Renamed to something like Home Archive & Story Recovery (working title), re‑angled around living people cataloging what matters instead of preparing for what comes later. Same service, honest frame, stops pulling your brand into elder care. This is the single biggest alignment gap between your vision and the current site.
30: 
31: WHAT I WOULDN'T TOUCH RIGHT NOW
32: 
33: The About bio. The fur coat, Gayle, the Joanne men — those stay yours to write when it's time. Not this week.
34: Well Dressed Citizen storefront. Do not build Shopify this month. It's a distraction from cash. The storefront is a 60‑day project after runway is stable.
35: The Companies / Patent / MAGIC / Podcast side stack. It's working. Leave it.
36: Pricing page structure. It's fine as a reference doc. Trust the text‑first CTA to carry the conversion instead.
37: What I need from you to start
38: 
39: Just four things:
40: 
41: Yes / no on Week 1. If yes, I start today with (1) text-first CTAs everywhere, (2) resale fast-path subline, (3) the $350 2‑hour House Call offer, (4) Cal.com/Calendly link you paste in, (5) Venmo/Zelle/Stripe handles you paste in. Most of that I can do without waiting — the payment handles I need from you.
42: Your Venmo and Zelle handles. (Don't paste them here — I'll add the fields once you tell me where.) Stripe I can link you to set up a payment link in 10 min.
43: Calendar link. If you don't have one, I'll set up the Cal.com free account config and you'll just sign in and confirm.

45: I'll do Tier 1 the moment you say go. Tier 2 the same week. Tier 3 only after Tier 1 is live and earning. Nothing gets built twice.

 27: ## 1. IDENTITY & VOICE
 28: 
 29: **Who you are in one sentence:**
 30: *The neighbor we don't have anymore — professionalized, in Los Angeles.*
 31: 
 32: **Voice rules (these are absolute):**
 33: - First person. Always.
 34: - Story-led. Specific objects, specific people. Never abstract benefits.
 35: - Calm, dry, warm. No hype. No "transform your life." No "girl, you got this."
 36: - Anti-Insta-perfect. *"I don't preach putting things in perfect spaces for the Instagram shot."*
 37: - No emojis on Facebook or Nextdoor. Maximum one tasteful emoji on Instagram, and only when it adds meaning.
 38: - Em-dashes are fine. Sentence fragments are fine. Half-finished thoughts that breathe — fine.
 39: - Never use "AWLC." Always **The Well Lived Citizen**. Full name. (Brand was renamed Apr 17, 2026 — dropped the "Co".)
 40: - Never say "Well Dressed Citizen LLC" on payments. Zelle is a phone/email handle.
 41: 
 42: **The five anchor stories (rotate forever, never wear out):**
 43: 1. **Gayle** — 84, post-hip surgery, the lamp clicker, Seattle, "she became one of the most independent women I've ever known."
 44: 2. **The flood** — 13 temporary homes/Airbnbs in a year, dog in the storage unit, "she was relief."
 45: 3. **The china** — incomplete sets, kids who said "that's sweet but no," what happens to the things you thought your family would always have.
 46: 4. **Stevie's capes / Steven Tyler's scarves** — objects holding identity, the museum glass moment, why this isn't decluttering.
 47: 5. **The baby shower mountain** — 8 months pregnant, hundreds of gifts, three of the same bouncer, no bandwidth.
 48: 
 49: **The headline that defines the brand:**
 50: > *Competence does not eliminate the need to be cared for.*
 51:

 56: ## 2. VISUAL SYSTEM
 57: 
 58: ### Color palette (locked, from your live site CSS — use these and only these on every post, asset, and graphic)
 59: 
 60: | Name | Hex | Use |
 61: |---|---|---|
 62: | **Cream** | `#F5F0E8` | Default backgrounds for posts |
 63: | **Warm** | `#FAF7F2` | Lightest background — hero areas, breathing room |
 64: | **Linen** | `#EDE7DB` | Card backgrounds, subtle dividers |
 65: | **Char** (charcoal) | `#1C1917` | Primary text, buttons, your strongest contrast |
 66: | **Ink** | `#292524` | Body text |
 67: | **Stone** | `#57534E` | Secondary text, captions |
 68: | **Clay** | `#78716C` | Tertiary text, metadata |
 69: | **Sand** | `#A8A29E` | Borders, very soft text |
 70: | **Rust** | `#9A5B3C` | Accent — links, key callouts, the warm "human" color |
 71: | **Rust soft** | `#B97A58` | Hover states, soft accents |
 72: 
 73: ### Typography
 74: - **Single font, everywhere:** **Plus Jakarta Sans** (free, Google Fonts).
 75: - Weights you actually use: 300, 400, 500, 600, 700. Italic 300 + 400 for occasional emphasis.
 76: - Don't introduce a second font. The whole brand reads as one voice partly *because* it sounds and looks like one voice.
 77: 
 78: ### Photography rules (the "anti-Instagram" rule made operational)
 79: - **Real spaces, real light.** Daylight if possible. Phone-quality is fine — preferred, even.
 80: - **One object per photo** when telling a story. The clicker. The plate. The folded coat. Not flatlays.
 81: - **Hands and small evidence.** Your hands packing, folding, holding. Backs of heads. No staged "founder portraits with arms crossed."
 82: - **Imperfect is the brand.** A half-folded pile, a counter mid-process, a real "before." Don't sanitize.
 83: - **Color tones to match the palette:** warm beige, cream, rust, charcoal. Avoid cold blues and high-saturation anything.
 84: 
 85: ### Logo / wordmark
 86: - Wordmark only: **The Well Lived Citizen** in Plus Jakarta Sans, weight 600, letter-spacing slightly open. Charcoal on cream. That's it. No icon. No flourishes.

161: ## 6. THE SITE — WHAT YOU CAN EDIT YOURSELF
162: 
163: ### What was built for you
164: A live business-info dashboard so you don't need an agent (or git, or files) to change phone numbers, email, hours, Zelle handles, Stripe links, etc.
165: 
166: - **URL:** your-site.com/admin.html
167: - **Password:** set via `ADMIN_PASSWORD` environment variable on the API server.
168: - **What it edits:** anything in `business-info.json` — phone, email, Zelle, Stripe link, social links, service area, hours.
169: - **How it works:** every page on your site auto-loads the latest values via `info-loader.js`. Edit once in admin → updates everywhere.
170: 
171: ### Important caveat (production)
172: - In **dev**, the admin saves to a file and persists.
173: - In **production**, file-based saves don't persist across deploys yet. The next upgrade is to move that to object storage so your edits survive forever. Flagged. To be done before you start changing things heavily on the live site.

263: - [ ] Get one testimonial. Gayle if she'll give one. Anyone. One line is enough. Put it on the homepage.
264: 
265: ### Week 3 — the positioning move
266: - [ ] Add one new band on the homepage, under the hero, ~80 words. The thesis: the gap, the neighbor we don't have, the trusted person you could actually call. (Draft on me, you keyword-edit, ship.)
267: - [ ] **Legacy → Home Archive & Story Recovery rename.** Re-angle toward living people cataloging what matters. Same service, honest frame, stops the elder-care drift.
268: - [ ] Migrate admin saves to object storage so production edits persist.
269: 
270: ---
271: 
272: ## 10. MONTHS 2-6 (long arc)
273: 
274: > Honest disclosure: only Weeks 1-3 + a 60-day storefront mention exist as saved strategy. Months 2-6 are extrapolated from the saved notes plus your knowledge base. Edit anything that's wrong.
275: 
276: ### Month 2 — runway stabilization
277: - The $350 House Call should be the steady cash floor by now. Goal: 4-6 House Calls per month. That is the bedrock.
278: - One full Resale pickup per week. Even small ones. The flow needs to become routine.
279: - Add one repeat House Call client to the **Flex Block** offer (continuity work — see knowledge base service definition).
280: - Start the **referral receipt** habit: every closed client gets the same ask: "If anyone you know would benefit, my number is the easiest way to send them my way."
281: 
282: ### Month 3 — credibility compounding
283: - Two more pinned site testimonials.
284: - "A few of the stories" page expands to 6-8 entries.
285: - Begin **Joanne men / fur coat publishing arc** — one essay per month, FB long-form first, then site, then IG carousel adaptation. This is the seed of the storefront's future merchandising voice. Don't rush.
286: - First Legacy/Home Archive project booked.
287: 
288: ### Month 4 — the storefront begins
289: - Open the Well Dressed Citizen storefront on Shopify. **Don't build before this.** The 60-day delay is intentional — you need the cash floor stable first.
290: - Begin with 10-15 highly curated pieces. Each piece has its story written in your voice. The storefront sells the *story*, not the inventory.
291: - Use the same color palette and font as the main site.
292: 
293: ### Month 5 — integration
294: - Patent / MAGIC / Podcast side stack: leave it running, but begin connecting it to the citizen brand on the **About** page only. One paragraph, no new section. Quiet credibility, not a separate tab.
295: - Hire your first 1099 helper for resale logistics (pickup, photography). Not for client-facing work. Protect the front door.
296: 
297: ### Month 6 — review and scale decision
298: - Run the numbers. House Calls/month, Resale gross/month, average ticket. You'll know whether to scale operations or hold and deepen.
299: - Decision moment: do you want to remain the only face of the brand, or train a second person who can be a "Citizen Concierge"? That's a real fork. Don't decide before Month 6.
300:

File: Visual-Brand-main/attached_assets/REDIRECT-VERIFICATION.md
================
 1: # Redirect Verification Checklist — welldressedcitizen.com → thewelllivedcitizen.com
 2: 
 3: Run this any time after a deploy to confirm the old domain still forwards to the live site.
 4: The redirect itself is configured at IONOS (domain forwarding), not in the website code.
 5: 
 6: ## A. Three curl commands (paste into Terminal)
 7: 
 8: Each should return a 301 or 302 with a `Location:` header pointing at `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/...`.
 9: 
10: ```bash
11: # 1. Bare apex
12: curl -sSI https://welldressedcitizen.com | grep -iE 'HTTP/|location'
13: 
14: # 2. www subdomain
15: curl -sSI https://www.welldressedcitizen.com | grep -iE 'HTTP/|location'
16: 
17: # 3. A nested path (proves path is preserved, not just root)
18: curl -sSI https://welldressedcitizen.com/services | grep -iE 'HTTP/|location'
19: ```
20: 
21: Expected output for each (status code may be 301 or 302):
22: 
23: ```
24: HTTP/2 301
25: location: https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/...
26: ```
27: 
28: ## B. Two browser checks
29: 
30: 1. Open a fresh private/incognito window. Go to `https://welldressedcitizen.com`.
31:    - Address bar should end up at `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/` and show the live site.
32: 2. In the same private window, go to `https://www.welldressedcitizen.com/contact`.
33:    - Address bar should end up at `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/contact` and show the contact page.
34: 
35: ## C. If any test above fails
36: 
37: 1. Sign in to IONOS → **Domains & SSL** → click `welldressedcitizen.com`.
38: 2. Open the **Destination** (or **Domain forwarding**) panel.
39: 3. Confirm:
40:    - Forwarding type: **HTTP redirect** (301 permanent).
41:    - Target URL: `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com`
42:    - "Forward subdomains" / "Forward paths" enabled so `/services` etc. are preserved.
43: 4. Save, wait ~5 minutes for DNS/redirect to propagate, then re-run section A.
44: 5. Also confirm `www.welldressedcitizen.com` either has the same forwarding rule or a CNAME pointing to the apex.
45: 
46: ## D. After all checks pass
47: 
48: Paste this URL into Google Search Console → **Sitemaps**:
49: 
50: ```
51: https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/sitemap.xml
52: ```

================
File: Visual-Brand-main/docs/submit-sitemap-to-google.md
================
 1: # Submit the Sitemap to Google Search Console
 2: 
 3: This guide walks you through verifying `thewelllivedcitizen.com` in Google Search Console and submitting the sitemap so new pages get discovered and indexed faster.
 4: 
 5: **Time required:** ~5 minutes (plus a few days for Google to finish indexing)
 6: 
 7: **Sitemap URL:** https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/sitemap.xml
 8: **Robots URL:** https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/robots.txt
 9: 
10: ---
11: 
12: ## Step 1 — Verify ownership of the domain
13: 
14: 1. Go to https://search.google.com/search-console
15: 2. Sign in with the Google account you want to manage the site with (use a permanent account, not a personal one you might lose access to).
16: 3. Click **Add property** in the top-left property selector.
17: 4. Choose one of the two verification methods:
18: 
19: ### Option A — Domain property (recommended)
20: Covers every subdomain and both http/https. Requires DNS access.
21: 
22: 1. Select **Domain** and enter: `thewelllivedcitizen.com`
23: 2. Click **Continue**. Google will display a **TXT record** that looks like:
24:    `google-site-verification=AbCdEf123...`
25: 3. Log in to your domain registrar (GoDaddy, Namecheap, Cloudflare, Google Domains, etc.).
26: 4. Open the DNS settings for `thewelllivedcitizen.com`.
27: 5. Add a new record:
28:    - **Type:** TXT
29:    - **Name / Host:** `@` (or leave blank — means the root domain)
30:    - **Value:** the full `google-site-verification=...` string Google gave you
31:    - **TTL:** default (usually 1 hour or 3600 seconds)
32: 6. Save the record. DNS propagation usually takes 5–30 minutes (occasionally up to a few hours).
33: 7. Return to Search Console and click **Verify**.
34: 
35: ### Option B — URL prefix property (easier, no DNS needed)
36: Covers only the exact URL prefix you enter.
37: 
38: 1. Select **URL prefix** and enter: `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com`
39: 2. Click **Continue**.
40: 3. Choose the **HTML tag** method. Google gives you a meta tag like:
41:    `<meta name="google-site-verification" content="AbCdEf123..." />`
42: 4. Send that tag to the developer (or paste it here in chat) so it can be added to the `<head>` of every page.
43: 5. Once the site is redeployed, click **Verify** in Search Console.
44: 
45: ---
46: 
47: ## Step 2 — Submit the sitemap
48: 
49: Once the property shows as verified:
50: 
51: 1. In the left sidebar, click **Sitemaps** (under the **Indexing** section).
52: 2. Under **Add a new sitemap**, type: `sitemap.xml`
53:    (The full URL field will auto-fill to `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/sitemap.xml`.)
54: 3. Click **Submit**.
55: 4. Within a minute or two, the **Status** column should change to **Success**.
56:    - If it shows **Couldn't fetch**, wait 10 minutes and refresh — Google sometimes retries automatically.
57:    - If it shows an error, open https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/sitemap.xml directly in your browser to confirm it loads.
58: 
59: ---
60: 
61: ## Step 3 — Confirm coverage (over the next few days)
62: 
63: Indexing isn't instant. Google will crawl in the background.
64: 
65: 1. In the left sidebar, click **Pages** (under **Indexing**).
66: 2. You should see all 9 public URLs listed as either:
67:    - **Indexed** — live in Google search
68:    - **Discovered – currently not indexed** — queued, will be indexed soon
69: 3. Initial indexing typically takes **2–14 days**. Re-check weekly.
70: 
71: ### Optional: request faster indexing for individual pages
72: 1. Use the **URL Inspection** bar at the top of Search Console.
73: 2. Paste a full URL (e.g. `https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services`).
74: 3. Click **Request Indexing**. Limit: ~10 requests per day.
75: 
76: ---
77: 
78: ## Done checklist
79: 
80: - [ ] Property added and verified in Search Console
81: - [ ] `sitemap.xml` submitted and showing **Success**
82: - [ ] Pages report shows all 9 URLs indexed or queued
83: 
84: ---
85: 
86: ## Troubleshooting
87: 
88: | Problem | Fix |
89: |---|---|
90: | "Verification failed" (Domain method) | DNS hasn't propagated yet. Wait 30 min and retry. Use https://dnschecker.org to confirm the TXT record is live. |
91: | "Couldn't fetch" sitemap | Open the sitemap URL in a browser to confirm it loads. Confirm `robots.txt` doesn't block Googlebot. |
92: | Pages stuck on "Discovered – currently not indexed" | Normal for new sites. Improves with backlinks and time. Use URL Inspection → Request Indexing for priority pages. |
93: | Lost access to verification | Add a second verified owner under **Settings → Users and permissions** as soon as you're verified, so access isn't tied to a single account. |

File: Visual-Brand-main/lib/api-client-react/src/generated/api.ts

 1: import { useQuery } from "@tanstack/react-query";
 2: import type {
 3:   QueryFunction,
 4:   QueryKey,
 5:   UseQueryOptions,
 6:   UseQueryResult,
 7: } from "@tanstack/react-query";
 8: import type { HealthStatus } from "./api.schemas";
 9: import { customFetch } from "../custom-fetch";
10: import type { ErrorType } from "../custom-fetch";
11: type AwaitedInput<T> = PromiseLike<T> | T;
12: type Awaited<O> = O extends AwaitedInput<infer T> ? T : never;
13: type SecondParameter<T extends (...args: never) => unknown> = Parameters<T>[1];
14: export const getHealthCheckUrl = () => {
15:   return `/api/healthz`;
16: };
17: export const healthCheck = async (
18:   options?: RequestInit,
19: ): Promise<HealthStatus> => {
20:   return customFetch<HealthStatus>(getHealthCheckUrl(), {
21:     ...options,
22:     method: "GET",
23:   });
24: };
25: export const getHealthCheckQueryKey = () => {
26:   return [`/api/healthz`] as const;
27: };
28: export const getHealthCheckQueryOptions = <
29:   TData = Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>,
30:   TError = ErrorType<unknown>,
31: >(options?: {
32:   query?: UseQueryOptions<
33:     Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>,
34:     TError,
35:     TData
36:   >;
37:   request?: SecondParameter<typeof customFetch>;
38: }) => {
39:   const { query: queryOptions, request: requestOptions } = options ?? {};
40:   const queryKey = queryOptions?.queryKey ?? getHealthCheckQueryKey();
41:   const queryFn: QueryFunction<Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>> = ({
42:     signal,
43:   }) => healthCheck({ signal, ...requestOptions });
44:   return { queryKey, queryFn, ...queryOptions } as UseQueryOptions<
45:     Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>,
46:     TError,
47:     TData
48:   > & { queryKey: QueryKey };
49: };
50: export type HealthCheckQueryResult = NonNullable<
51:   Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>
52: >;
53: export type HealthCheckQueryError = ErrorType<unknown>;
54: export function useHealthCheck<
55:   TData = Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>,
56:   TError = ErrorType<unknown>,
57: >(options?: {
58:   query?: UseQueryOptions<
59:     Awaited<ReturnType<typeof healthCheck>>,
60:     TError,
61:     TData
62:   >;
63:   request?: SecondParameter<typeof customFetch>;
64: }): UseQueryResult<TData, TError> & { queryKey: QueryKey } {
65:   const queryOptions = getHealthCheckQueryOptions(options);
66:   const query = useQuery(queryOptions) as UseQueryResult<TData, TError> & {
67:     queryKey: QueryKey;
68:   };
69:   return { ...query, queryKey: queryOptions.queryKey };
70: }

================
File: Visual-Brand-main/lib/api-client-react/src/custom-fetch.ts
================
  1: export type CustomFetchOptions = RequestInit & {
  2:   responseType?: "json" | "text" | "blob" | "auto";
  3: };
  4: export type ErrorType<T = unknown> = ApiError<T>;
  5: export type BodyType<T> = T;
  6: export type AuthTokenGetter = () => Promise<string | null> | string | null;
  7: const NO_BODY_STATUS = new Set([204, 205, 304]);
  8: const DEFAULT_JSON_ACCEPT = "application/json, application/problem+json";
  9: let _baseUrl: string | null = null;
 10: let _authTokenGetter: AuthTokenGetter | null = null;
 11: export function setBaseUrl(url: string | null): void {
 12:   _baseUrl = url ? url.replace(/\/+$/, "") : null;
 13: }
 14: /**
 15:  * Register a getter that supplies a bearer auth token.  Before every fetch
 16:  * the getter is invoked; when it returns a non-null string, an
 17:  * `Authorization: Bearer <token>` header is attached to the request.
 18:  *
 19:  * Useful for Expo bundles making token-gated API calls.
 20:  * Pass `null` to clear the getter.
 21:  *
 22:  * NOTE: This function should never be used in web applications where session
 23:  * token cookies are automatically associated with API calls by the browser.
 24:  */
 25: export function setAuthTokenGetter(getter: AuthTokenGetter | null): void {
 26:   _authTokenGetter = getter;
 27: }
 28: function isRequest(input: RequestInfo | URL): input is Request {
 29:   return typeof Request !== "undefined" && input instanceof Request;
 30: }
 31: function resolveMethod(input: RequestInfo | URL, explicitMethod?: string): string {
 32:   if (explicitMethod) return explicitMethod.toUpperCase();
 33:   if (isRequest(input)) return input.method.toUpperCase();
 34:   return "GET";
 35: }
 36: function isUrl(input: RequestInfo | URL): input is URL {
 37:   return typeof URL !== "undefined" && input instanceof URL;
 38: }
 39: function applyBaseUrl(input: RequestInfo | URL): RequestInfo | URL {
 40:   if (!_baseUrl) return input;
 41:   const url = resolveUrl(input);
 42:   if (!url.startsWith("/")) return input;
 43:   const absolute = `${_baseUrl}${url}`;
 44:   if (typeof input === "string") return absolute;
 45:   if (isUrl(input)) return new URL(absolute);
 46:   return new Request(absolute, input as Request);
 47: }
 48: function resolveUrl(input: RequestInfo | URL): string {
 49:   if (typeof input === "string") return input;
 50:   if (isUrl(input)) return input.toString();
 51:   return input.url;
 52: }
 53: function mergeHeaders(...sources: Array<HeadersInit | undefined>): Headers {
 54:   const headers = new Headers();
 55:   for (const source of sources) {
 56:     if (!source) continue;
 57:     new Headers(source).forEach((value, key) => {
 58:       headers.set(key, value);
 59:     });
 60:   }
 61:   return headers;
 62: }
 63: function getMediaType(headers: Headers): string | null {
 64:   const value = headers.get("content-type");
 65:   return value ? value.split(";", 1)[0].trim().toLowerCase() : null;
 66: }
 67: function isJsonMediaType(mediaType: string | null): boolean {
 68:   return mediaType === "application/json" || Boolean(mediaType?.endsWith("+json"));
 69: }
 70: function isTextMediaType(mediaType: string | null): boolean {
 71:   return Boolean(
 72:     mediaType &&
 73:       (mediaType.startsWith("text/") ||
 74:         mediaType === "application/xml" ||
 75:         mediaType === "text/xml" ||
 76:         mediaType.endsWith("+xml") ||
 77:         mediaType === "application/x-www-form-urlencoded"),
 78:   );
 79: }
 80: function hasNoBody(response: Response, method: string): boolean {
 81:   if (method === "HEAD") return true;
 82:   if (NO_BODY_STATUS.has(response.status)) return true;
 83:   if (response.headers.get("content-length") === "0") return true;
 84:   if (response.body === null) return true;
 85:   return false;
 86: }
 87: function stripBom(text: string): string {
 88:   return text.charCodeAt(0) === 0xfeff ? text.slice(1) : text;
 89: }
 90: function looksLikeJson(text: string): boolean {
 91:   const trimmed = text.trimStart();
 92:   return trimmed.startsWith("{") || trimmed.startsWith("[");
 93: }
 94: function getStringField(value: unknown, key: string): string | undefined {
 95:   if (!value || typeof value !== "object") return undefined;
 96:   const candidate = (value as Record<string, unknown>)[key];
 97:   if (typeof candidate !== "string") return undefined;
 98:   const trimmed = candidate.trim();
 99:   return trimmed === "" ? undefined : trimmed;
100: }
101: function truncate(text: string, maxLength = 300): string {
102:   return text.length > maxLength ? `${text.slice(0, maxLength - 1)}…` : text;
103: }
104: function buildErrorMessage(response: Response, data: unknown): string {
105:   const prefix = `HTTP ${response.status} ${response.statusText}`;
106:   if (typeof data === "string") {
107:     const text = data.trim();
108:     return text ? `${prefix}: ${truncate(text)}` : prefix;
109:   }
110:   const title = getStringField(data, "title");
111:   const detail = getStringField(data, "detail");
112:   const message =
113:     getStringField(data, "message") ??
114:     getStringField(data, "error_description") ??
115:     getStringField(data, "error");
116:   if (title && detail) return `${prefix}: ${title} — ${detail}`;
117:   if (detail) return `${prefix}: ${detail}`;
118:   if (message) return `${prefix}: ${message}`;
119:   if (title) return `${prefix}: ${title}`;
120:   return prefix;
121: }
122: export class ApiError<T = unknown> extends Error {
123:   readonly name = "ApiError";
124:   readonly status: number;
125:   readonly statusText: string;
126:   readonly data: T | null;
127:   readonly headers: Headers;
128:   readonly response: Response;
129:   readonly method: string;
130:   readonly url: string;
131:   constructor(
132:     response: Response,
133:     data: T | null,
134:     requestInfo: { method: string; url: string },
135:   ) {
136:     super(buildErrorMessage(response, data));
137:     Object.setPrototypeOf(this, new.target.prototype);
138:     this.status = response.status;
139:     this.statusText = response.statusText;
140:     this.data = data;
141:     this.headers = response.headers;
142:     this.response = response;
143:     this.method = requestInfo.method;
144:     this.url = response.url || requestInfo.url;
145:   }
146: }
147: export class ResponseParseError extends Error {
148:   readonly name = "ResponseParseError";
149:   readonly status: number;
150:   readonly statusText: string;
151:   readonly headers: Headers;
152:   readonly response: Response;
153:   readonly method: string;
154:   readonly url: string;
155:   readonly rawBody: string;
156:   readonly cause: unknown;
157:   constructor(
158:     response: Response,
159:     rawBody: string,
160:     cause: unknown,
161:     requestInfo: { method: string; url: string },
162:   ) {
163:     super(
164:       `Failed to parse response from ${requestInfo.method} ${response.url || requestInfo.url} ` +
165:         `(${response.status} ${response.statusText}) as JSON`,
166:     );
167:     Object.setPrototypeOf(this, new.target.prototype);
168:     this.status = response.status;
169:     this.statusText = response.statusText;
170:     this.headers = response.headers;
171:     this.response = response;
172:     this.method = requestInfo.method;
173:     this.url = response.url || requestInfo.url;
174:     this.rawBody = rawBody;
175:     this.cause = cause;
176:   }
177: }
178: async function parseJsonBody(
179:   response: Response,
180:   requestInfo: { method: string; url: string },
181: ): Promise<unknown> {
182:   const raw = await response.text();
183:   const normalized = stripBom(raw);
184:   if (normalized.trim() === "") {
185:     return null;
186:   }
187:   try {
188:     return JSON.parse(normalized);
189:   } catch (cause) {
190:     throw new ResponseParseError(response, raw, cause, requestInfo);
191:   }
192: }
193: async function parseErrorBody(response: Response, method: string): Promise<unknown> {
194:   if (hasNoBody(response, method)) {
195:     return null;
196:   }
197:   const mediaType = getMediaType(response.headers);
198:   // Fall back to text when blob() is unavailable (e.g. some React Native builds).
199:   if (mediaType && !isJsonMediaType(mediaType) && !isTextMediaType(mediaType)) {
200:     return typeof response.blob === "function" ? response.blob() : response.text();
201:   }
202:   const raw = await response.text();
203:   const normalized = stripBom(raw);
204:   const trimmed = normalized.trim();
205:   if (trimmed === "") {
206:     return null;
207:   }
208:   if (isJsonMediaType(mediaType) || looksLikeJson(normalized)) {
209:     try {
210:       return JSON.parse(normalized);
211:     } catch {
212:       return raw;
213:     }
214:   }
215:   return raw;
216: }
217: function inferResponseType(response: Response): "json" | "text" | "blob" {
218:   const mediaType = getMediaType(response.headers);
219:   if (isJsonMediaType(mediaType)) return "json";
220:   if (isTextMediaType(mediaType) || mediaType == null) return "text";
221:   return "blob";
222: }
223: async function parseSuccessBody(
224:   response: Response,
225:   responseType: "json" | "text" | "blob" | "auto",
226:   requestInfo: { method: string; url: string },
227: ): Promise<unknown> {
228:   if (hasNoBody(response, requestInfo.method)) {
229:     return null;
230:   }
231:   const effectiveType =
232:     responseType === "auto" ? inferResponseType(response) : responseType;
233:   switch (effectiveType) {
234:     case "json":
235:       return parseJsonBody(response, requestInfo);
236:     case "text": {
237:       const text = await response.text();
238:       return text === "" ? null : text;
239:     }
240:     case "blob":
241:       if (typeof response.blob !== "function") {
242:         throw new TypeError(
243:           "Blob responses are not supported in this runtime. " +
244:             "Use responseType \"json\" or \"text\" instead.",
245:         );
246:       }
247:       return response.blob();
248:   }
249: }
250: export async function customFetch<T = unknown>(
251:   input: RequestInfo | URL,
252:   options: CustomFetchOptions = {},
253: ): Promise<T> {
254:   input = applyBaseUrl(input);
255:   const { responseType = "auto", headers: headersInit, ...init } = options;
256:   const method = resolveMethod(input, init.method);
257:   if (init.body != null && (method === "GET" || method === "HEAD")) {
258:     throw new TypeError(`customFetch: ${method} requests cannot have a body.`);
259:   }
260:   const headers = mergeHeaders(isRequest(input) ? input.headers : undefined, headersInit);
261:   if (
262:     typeof init.body === "string" &&
263:     !headers.has("content-type") &&
264:     looksLikeJson(init.body)
265:   ) {
266:     headers.set("content-type", "application/json");
267:   }
268:   if (responseType === "json" && !headers.has("accept")) {
269:     headers.set("accept", DEFAULT_JSON_ACCEPT);
270:   }
271:   if (_authTokenGetter && !headers.has("authorization")) {
272:     const token = await _authTokenGetter();
273:     if (token) {
274:       headers.set("authorization", `Bearer ${token}`);
275:     }
276:   }
277:   const requestInfo = { method, url: resolveUrl(input) };
278:   const response = await fetch(input, { ...init, method, headers });
279:   if (!response.ok) {
280:     const errorData = await parseErrorBody(response, method);
281:     throw new ApiError(response, errorData, requestInfo);
282:   }
283:   return (await parseSuccessBody(response, responseType, requestInfo)) as T;
284: }

  1: # The Well Lived Citizen — Project Context
  2: 
  3: > **READ THIS FIRST.** This file loads automatically into every agent's memory. It is the orientation any future agent (or future-me) needs before touching anything.
  4: 
  5: ---
  6: 
  7: ## WHO THIS IS FOR
  8: 
  9: **Owner:** Dayna Brown
 10: **Location:** Los Angeles
 11: **Phone:** (323) 433-1350 — primary CTA across the entire brand
 12: **Email:** dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com
 13: **Site:** thewelllivedcitizen.com (no "co" — confirmed Apr 17, 2026 against the live published endpoint)
 14: 
 15: Dayna is the operator. She is **not technical**: she does not use git, JSON, or files directly. She works visually and conversationally. She edits her business info through `admin.html`, not the codebase. Anything you generate in chat that is not saved to a file is **lost to her**. Default to writing real files.
 16: 
 17: ---
 18: 
 19: ## WHAT THIS PROJECT IS
 20: 
 21: **The Well Lived Citizen** — a Los Angeles concierge / home-organization / legacy / resale service. Multi-page static site (Vite) + Express API server. The site is the front door; the phone number is the actual conversion point.
 22: 
 23: **Brand-name history (do not re-litigate):** The brand was renamed from "The Well Lived Citizen Co" to "The Well Lived Citizen" in commit `7935067` on Apr 17, 2026. The social handles were also renamed late that same night to drop the "co": Company IG/FB went from `@thewelllivedcitizenco` to `@thewelllivedcitizen`; Closet IG went from `@thewelllivedcitizencocloset` to `@thewelllivedcloset` (note: also dropped "citizen"). The archive account `@welldressedcitizen` is unchanged. The eBay store `thewelllivedclosetco` retains the "co" deliberately. The Poshmark closet is `welllivedcloset`. Any reference to ".co" or "Citizen Co" anywhere in the project, outside the LLC name (`Well Dressed Citizen LLC`) and the eBay store username, is **drift** and must be corrected, not propagated.
 24: 
 25: ### Tech stack
 26: - Monorepo: pnpm workspace
 27: - Site: `artifacts/website/` — static HTML + CSS, no framework, served by Vite
 28: - API: `artifacts/api-server/` — Express 5, TypeScript, esbuild bundle
 29: - Storage: `artifacts/api-server/data/business-info.json` (file-based; production-persistence is a known gap, see below)
 30: - Auth: simple `ADMIN_PASSWORD` env var on the API server gates the admin save
 31: 
 32: ### Three workflows
 33: 1. `artifacts/api-server: API Server` — port 8080
 34: 2. `artifacts/mockup-sandbox: Component Preview Server` — port 8081
 35: 3. `artifacts/website: web` — Vite dev server
 36: 
 37: ### Backups
 38: - **GitHub remote configured but NOT pushed:** `https://github.com/dbrownla5/Visual-Brand-Boost` is set as `origin` but Replit is not authenticated to push to it. The repo on GitHub is empty. To fix: operator opens Replit Tools → Git → Connect to GitHub, authorizes, selects existing repo, pushes. All local commits then sync up.
 39: - **Replit gitsafe-backup** (automatic local mirror) — this IS active and current.
 40: - **Replit Deployment** — the live site is published independently and survives even if the workspace is wiped.
 41: - **47 agent memory snapshots** at `.local/state/replit/agent/.agent_state_*.bin` (restorable via Replit History panel).
 42: 
 43: ---
 44: 
 45: ## BRAND VOICE — non-negotiable
 46: 
 47: Voice is the single most important thing on this project. **Almost every other failure on this project has been a voice failure.**
 48: 
 49: - **First person, always.** Story-led. Specific objects, specific people. Never abstract benefits.
 50: - **Calm, dry, warm.** Anti-hustle. No hype. No "transform your life." No emojis on Facebook/Nextdoor; max one tasteful one on Instagram.
 51: - **Anti-Insta-perfect.** Real spaces, real light, mid-process imperfection. Phone-quality photos preferred over staged.
 52: - **Em-dashes are fine. Sentence fragments are fine.**
 53: - **Never use "AWLC."** Always full name: **The Well Lived Citizen** (no "Co" since the Apr 17 rename).
 54: - **Never say "Well Dressed Citizen LLC" on payments.** Zelle uses phone/email handles only.
 55: - **Phone format is exactly `(323) 433-1350`.** Never reformatted.
 56: 
 57: ### The headline that defines the brand
 58: > *Competence does not eliminate the need to be cared for.*
 59: 
 60: If something you write doesn't sit comfortably next to that sentence, rewrite it.
 61: 
 62: ### Five anchor stories (locked source-of-truth in the knowledge base)
 63: 1. Gayle (84, post-hip surgery, the lamp clicker, Seattle)
 64: 2. The flood (13 temporary homes / Airbnbs in a year, dog in storage, "she was relief")
 65: 3. The china (incomplete sets, kids who said no)
 66: 4. Stevie's capes / Steven Tyler's scarves (museum glass, objects holding identity)
 67: 5. The baby shower mountain (8 months pregnant, hundreds of gifts)
 68: 
 69: ---
 70: 
 71: ## THE FOUR PILLARS
 72: 
 73: | # | Pillar | Notes |
 74: |---|---|---|
 75: | 1 | Home Organization & Modern Move | Stable. Don't touch positioning. |
 76: | 2 | Legacy Planning & Inventory Catalog | **Slated to rename to "Home Archive & Story Recovery" in Week 3** — re-angle toward living people cataloging what matters, not preparing for the end. Stops the elder-care drift. |
 77: | 3 | House Calls | **Soft-launch positioning:** productize as "2-hour House Call — $350, book this week." Fixed price, calendar link, one-tap. |
 78: | 4 | Curated Resale & Consignment | **Soft-launch positioning:** lead with photo fast-path, not the agreement. "Send a photo to (323) 433-1350. I'll quote pickup. Agreement only after you see the number." |
 79: 
 80: ---
 81: 
 82: ## DECISION LOCKS — do NOT change
 83: 
 84: 1. No "AWLC" — always full brand name.
 85: 2. Phone format exactly `(323) 433-1350`.
 86: 3. Online resale: all sales final, no chargebacks. Never soften.
 87: 4. In-person tone is warm; online resale tone is strict. Two voices on purpose.
 88: 5. No fixed pricing tier for larger estates. Whole-Home & Extended-Complex Legacy must be quoted after walkthrough.
 89: 6. No "Special Delivery" as a separate service line — that's House Calls content.
 90: 7. No Shopify storefront before Month 4. Cash floor first.
 91: 8. No Thumbtack, no TaskRabbit, no platform-feed services.
 92: 9. **Plus Jakarta Sans is the only font.** Don't add a second.
 93: 10. Color palette in `style.css` (`--cream`, `--warm`, `--linen`, `--char`, `--ink`, `--stone`, `--clay`, `--sand`, `--rust`, `--rust-soft`) is the only palette.
 94:

 97: ## CRITICAL PENDING / KNOWN ISSUES
 98: 
 99: - **Admin saves don't persist in production yet.** `business-info.json` is file-based; surviving deploys requires moving to object storage. Flagged for Week 3.
100: - **No Stripe payment link** wired in yet. `business-info.json` has slots; Dayna needs to create a Stripe payment link and the URL gets pasted in.
101: - **No Cal.com / Calendly link** wired in yet. Required for the $350 House Call to function as one-tap booking.
102: - **Hero CTAs and conversion blocks on `index.html`** still funnel to the contact form (`contact.html`). The Week-1 plan calls for text-first CTAs (`sms:` links with prefilled body). Not yet implemented — pending operator OK.
103: - **Resale card** still says "Commission-based · agreement required" without the photo-fast-path subline. Pending operator OK.

Recovered from the prior strategy session. **This supersedes anything in `10-day-launch-content.md`.**
112: 2. `attached_assets/welllivedcitizen_knowledge_base_1776369478910.json` — locked brand voice, pillar copy, headlines, anchor stories. Used for site copy and the *raw materials* that the marketing program shapes.

114: 4. `attached_assets/PLAYBOOK.md` — operator playbook. **Caveat:** portions extrapolated past saved strategy; verify against the marketing program above for any social/voice question.
115: 5. `attached_assets/10-day-launch-content.md` — **DEPRECATED. Do not use.** Written before the brand-match marketing program was recovered. Operator rejected it. Use the four launch posts in BRAND-MATCH-MARKETING-PROGRAM.md instead.
116: 6. `attached_assets/SESSION-AUDIT-and-TIMELINE.md` — full record of all checkpoints, backups, recovery paths.
117: 7. `attached_assets/DAYNABROWN_EXPERIENCE_V_1776375994228.docx` — operator's professional experience.
118: 8. `artifacts/api-server/data/business-info.json` — editable business info (powers site via `info-loader.js`).

120: ## DIVISION OF LABOR — who does what
121: 
122: - **Dayna runs all content.** She decides what gets written, by whom, when. Manus is one of her tools assisting her — not a co-owner, not a separate channel to coordinate with.
123: - **This project's job:** the website, the API, site copy, and whatever Dayna explicitly asks for. Don't volunteer to draft closet captions, social posts, or piece copy unless she asks.
124: - **Domain / DNS / SSL / IONOS:** Dayna handles directly. Don't ask, don't offer.
125: - **Today (launch day):** stay in lane. Execute what's asked. Don't spin up extra work.
126: 
127: ## THREE-ACCOUNT ARCHITECTURE (memorize this)
128: 
129: | Handle | Role | Voice notes |
130: |---|---|---|
131: | `@thewelllivedcitizen` | Company — positioning + lead gen | Calm, observant, dry, slightly literary. Sentence case. No exclamations. |
132: | `@thewelllivedcloset` | Closet — Poshmark/eBay sales + intake. **The cash account.** | Same register, more connoisseur. Story-led, never bargain-led. |
133: | `@welldressedcitizen` | Archive — one transition post then dark | Brief, warm, final. |
134: 
135: **Cross-tag rule:** Company and Closet feed each other via @-mentions in every relevant post. Never post the same item to both on the same day.

138: 
139: ## WORKING WITH DAYNA — operating notes
140: 
141: - **She is exhausted and pre-launch.** Match her urgency without performing.
142: - **Do not regurgitate the knowledge base back at her.** She can tell. It reads as "GPT echo." Drafts that pull anchor stories at her without her in the room have been rejected.
143: - **Don't ask diagnostic questions when you can do the work.** "Should I X or Y?" wastes her time. Pick one, do it, show, adjust.
144: - **Don't apologize repeatedly.** It registers as performance. Acknowledge once, move.
145: - **Save things to files by default.** Anything generated only in chat is lost to her.
146: - **Voice rewrites need her in the room.** The kb gives you the vocabulary; only she gives you the cadence.
147: - **She has been burned by previous sessions losing strategic conversation.** Restoring a checkpoint via Replit's History panel (clock icon) is the only way to recover prior chat memory — direct her there for anything that "feels missing."
